<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_26dee597-db83-46c4-bbf6-252388acac62'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer11284743705971892386">Edward Rutherfurd celebrates America’s greatest city in a rich, engrossing saga, weaving together tales of families rich and poor, native-born and immigrant—a cast of fictional and true characters whose fates rise and fall and rise again with the city’s fortunes. From this intimate perspective we see New York’s humble beginnings as a tiny Indian fishing village, the arriva</span>
  <span id="freeText11284743705971892386" style="display:none">Edward Rutherfurd celebrates America’s greatest city in a rich, engrossing saga, weaving together tales of families rich and poor, native-born and immigrant—a cast of fictional and true characters whose fates rise and fall and rise again with the city’s fortunes. From this intimate perspective we see New York’s humble beginnings as a tiny Indian fishing village, the arrival of Dutch and British merchants, the Revolutionary War, the emergence of the city as a great trading and financial center, the convulsions of the Civil War, the excesses of the Gilded Age, the explosion of immigration in the late nineteenth and early twentieth centuries, the trials of World War II, the near demise of New York in the 1970s and its roaring rebirth in the 1990s, and the attack on the World Trade Center. A stirring mix of battle, romance, family struggles, and personal triumphs, <b>New York: The Novel</b> gloriously captures the search for freedom and opportunity at the heart of our nation’s history.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11284743705971892386" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/182688-anyone-have-an-anecdote-from-ancestors">Anyone have an anecdote from ancestors about the Great Influenza Pandemic of 1918? Some called it the Spanish Flu because of the publicity that came from Spain about it. The rest of Eurpoe was too busy fighting WWI to report on flu.</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_182688'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F8258519-new-york">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/17173472-marie-baird"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1456416768i/17173472._UY100_CR16,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/17173472-marie-baird">Marie Baird</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">My grandfather (a Canadian WW1 soldier) and my grandmother (a London girl) were married in London, England on November 11, 1918 (the day we've come to<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">My grandfather (a Canadian WW1 soldier) and my grandmother (a London girl) were married in London, England on November 11, 1918 (the day we've come to recognize as the Armistice Day). My grandfather's best man (who looks rather thin and warn in the formal wedding photo) died two days later of the influenza. It's a story that's been passed down in our family by my grandpa and then my mother. The wedding photo has always had a rather haunting quality for me ... knowing, from the distance of time, what would be the fates of many of the individuals pictured there. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lori" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lori" href="/user/show/68050592-lori">Lori</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/8696944-new-york">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2543905963" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11615480569861115545">Reminds me of James Michener. <br/><br/>It’s billed as assessable history, so depending on your base line parts seem rushed and lite. In places the research shows like the opposite of an actor giving a seamless performance. But, he covers a lot of territory from angels I don’t often read—Lincoln’s Gettysburg Address from a press photographer’s point of view.<br/><br/>Follows a prospering mostly WASP family from New Amsterdam to post-911. Their name is Masters. Stop rolling your eyes if they get stuck looking into t</span>
  <span id="freeText11615480569861115545" style="display:none">Reminds me of James Michener. <br /><br />It’s billed as assessable history, so depending on your base line parts seem rushed and lite. In places the research shows like the opposite of an actor giving a seamless performance. But, he covers a lot of territory from angels I don’t often read—Lincoln’s Gettysburg Address from a press photographer’s point of view.<br /><br />Follows a prospering mostly WASP family from New Amsterdam to post-911. Their name is Masters. Stop rolling your eyes if they get stuck looking into the back of your head then you can’t read anymore. <br /><br />There are other families to illustrate slavery, natives, and immigration. No point in getting to attached to any of them for the most part they’ll be gone in a few chapters. There are wars to prosper from and fires to fight. The city is the star no matter which story line your following.<br /><br />I loved those independent Dutch women.<br /><br />**********************************************************<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.kirkusreviews.com/book-reviews/edward-rutherfurd/new-york-4/">https://www.kirkusreviews.com/book-re...</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.thenewdorkreviewofbooks.com/2010/06/new-york-book-review.html">https://www.thenewdorkreviewofbooks.c...</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.washingtonpost.com/wp-dyn/content/article/2009/12/07/AR2009120703778.html?noredirect=on">http://www.washingtonpost.com/wp-dyn/...</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11615480569861115545" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2085142468" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2085142468" />
    <a title="Jackie Ullerich" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5841822-jackie-ullerich"><img alt="Jackie Ullerich" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311277988p2/5841822.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2085142468?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jackie Ullerich" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jackie Ullerich" href="/user/show/5841822-jackie-ullerich">Jackie Ullerich</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2085142468" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4417403449015635161">Edward Rutherfurd is an exceptional historical fiction author. His attention to details, the character development, the emotion, the settings, the multi-generations bring his books to life. If historical fiction is a genre you love and you haven't read any of his books yet, it's a must. And perhaps <i>New York</i> is the perfect Rutherfurd novel to start with.<br/><br/>Why?<br/>1. It's told in sequence, no jumping from the past to the present like in <i>Paris</i>, so it might be easier to follow for some. The novel starts w</span>
  <span id="freeText4417403449015635161" style="display:none">Edward Rutherfurd is an exceptional historical fiction author. His attention to details, the character development, the emotion, the settings, the multi-generations bring his books to life. If historical fiction is a genre you love and you haven't read any of his books yet, it's a must. And perhaps <i>New York</i> is the perfect Rutherfurd novel to start with.<br /><br />Why?<br />1. It's told in sequence, no jumping from the past to the present like in <i>Paris</i>, so it might be easier to follow for some. The novel starts when New York was called New Amsterdam and ends in the 1960's. Long before skyscrapers, there was a wildness, a wickedness, and Rutherfurd does an outstanding job of sharing the good, the bad, the ugly, the touching, the heartbreak, the hope, the love and passion.<br />2. The characters are incredibly fascinating and you'll want to follow their lives.<br />3. Despite the length of this novel, it's an easy read.<br />4. Multi-generational with appearances by famous Americans.<br />5. Relatable. Even if you've never been to New York, New York is a place Americans know. But I've also learned through my travels around the world that many people from other countries equate New York to America. It is by far our most iconic city, and this is an opportunity to learn so much more. <br /><br />Highly recommend! <br /><br />I looking forward to Rutherfurd's <i>China</i>, which will be coming out in 2018! I'm really curious about it. How will he handle an entire country?</span>
  <a data-text-id="4417403449015635161" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1756459375" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1756459375" />
    <a title="Elyse  Walters" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/597461-elyse-walters"><img alt="Elyse  Walters" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514246949p2/597461.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1756459375?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elyse  Walters" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elyse  Walters" href="/user/show/597461-elyse-walters">Elyse  Walters</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1756459375" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7714806523061757797">Audiobook/sync with my ebook.<br/>Mark Bramhall was the narrator of the Audiobook....( 37 hours and 17 minutes long)....shorter if interchanging with ebook-reading. <br/><br/>An 860 page historical fiction book is not a zippy-quickie read. <br/>Yet....it’s the type of book that gives a reader a glow of pride when finishing it. <br/><br/>Edward Rutherfurd, has a reputation for being KING of HISTORICAL FICTION writing. Well, “New York” is definitely exceptional, that’s for sure. <br/>I’ve been wanting to read Rutherfurd’s books for</span>
  <span id="freeText7714806523061757797" style="display:none">Audiobook/sync with my ebook.<br />Mark Bramhall was the narrator of the Audiobook....( 37 hours and 17 minutes long)....shorter if interchanging with ebook-reading. <br /><br />An 860 page historical fiction book is not a zippy-quickie read. <br />Yet....it’s the type of book that gives a reader a glow of pride when finishing it. <br /><br />Edward Rutherfurd, has a reputation for being KING of HISTORICAL FICTION writing. Well, “New York” is definitely exceptional, that’s for sure. <br />I’ve been wanting to read Rutherfurd’s books for 20 years! Finally.... and now that I’ve gotten my feet wet and tested the waters.... I’m even more excited to read other Rutherfurd books... thinking “London” might be my next choice. <br /><br />I LOVED THE PUGNACIOUS &amp; POLYCHROMATIC CHARACTERS!!!(like those juicy words?)....<br />Ha....well, the characters ‘are’ juicy interesting! <br /><br />Doesn’t everyone have a New York story....or two or three? <br />Ha....my very first trip to New York was when I was 18 years old. <br />I was alone on my way to Israel. I had a scary first night in New York — I was being followed by a Frenchman who had been sitting next to me on a bus. It was late, and dark. After landing at Kennedy airport. I took a bus into Manhattan needing to find a place to sleep. The next day I was leaving for Israel. <br />I got off the bus. Frenchman got off too and started following me... I started running. He started running. I started crying ... I didn’t look back to see if he was crying. I quickly ran into a hotel that was way more expensive than I could afford. Shaking with tears- the desk man gave me a free room to stay for the night. I’ll always be thankful for his kind generosity. It felt like he saved my life! I was ‘that’ scared. <br />I hadn’t had food all day. I managed to sleep a little that night - tummy growling- still scare - but wouldn’t leave my room until early the next morning....I got up early, headed back to the airport. I sat in the busy airport all day -but felt safe there -until my next plane took off. <br />I’ve had many more memorable pleasurable experiences in New York since that first visit. I even worked in New York in my<br />mid -20’s. I enjoyed my morning runs through Central Park before work. <br /><br />Love to know about others 1st time walking the streets in NYC!!!!<br /><br />I chose this book - now - as my way ( silly I suppose)... to give thanks to governor Andrew Cuomo, who for me has been one of my favorite leaders to follow, listen to.... during these coronavirus days. He’s the only leader who has made me cry THANK YOU tears ‘while’ getting briefings. <br />Trump just makes me WANT TO SCREAM.<br />But blessings for Cuomo —— and a big thank you to NEW YORK! I have fallen into Cuomo’s hands for ‘truth’ reporting. <br />My deep sympathy to<br />the many people who have died — and their families hurting from their loss. <br />Many thanks to the health workers and every employee- grocery stores- etc. who continue to put their lives at risk every day due to their essential jobs.<br /><br />New York has had more than its share of devastating blows. <br />The storytelling in this book felt like a great tribute to the generations and generations of the courageous men and women in New York that refuse to be victimized. <br /><br />There are already thousands of reviews of this book, so not sure what else I need to add other than I enjoyed it!!<br /><br />It was easy to get wrapped up with the compelling characters — the descriptions—the early days of slavery, followed by ongoing chronological highlights of history.<br /><br />The fiction characters felt like real people—most likable dealing with challenging life situations. <br />I became attached to a few of the characters, right away.<br /><br />Rutherfurd added new characters delicately — allowing time to get get to know them. <br />We meet many diverse families [Multiculturalism at its best]...The Dutch, and their English heritage, Native Americans, Irish, German, Italian, German-Jewish, and Puerto Rican immigrants....from 1664 to 2011—ending with 9/11....<br />written from the perspective of the Dutch settlers. <br />We visit the wars: the American revolution, the Civil War, World War I, World War II, and the wars between family members. <br /><br />Incredibly ambitious and fabulously written....<br />a book worth spending time with.....<br />Honoring love for the great city of New York!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7714806523061757797" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_90059576" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/90059576" />
    <a title="Sean Kennedy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2535186-sean-kennedy"><img alt="Sean Kennedy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442482458p2/2535186.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/90059576?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Kennedy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Kennedy" href="/user/show/2535186-sean-kennedy">Sean Kennedy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385521383" href="/book/show/6257535-new-york">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer90059576" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8262287664174818533">I like reading somewhat trashy historical family sagas, but I was expecting a little more diversity in this book following four centuries of the history of New York and the people who lived in it. After all, New York is a hubub of multiculturalism, but this book ends up being overwhelmingly Anglocentric. The African-American family disappear halfway through the story, the Italians get a few chapters and then only a few cameos, and the Puerto Ricans just a few appearances as the 'friends' of the </span>
  <span id="freeText8262287664174818533" style="display:none">I like reading somewhat trashy historical family sagas, but I was expecting a little more diversity in this book following four centuries of the history of New York and the people who lived in it. After all, New York is a hubub of multiculturalism, but this book ends up being overwhelmingly Anglocentric. The African-American family disappear halfway through the story, the Italians get a few chapters and then only a few cameos, and the Puerto Ricans just a few appearances as the 'friends' of the main character at the end. The story is also extremely choppy - as I guess a 1000 page novel dealing with four hundred years would be - but it seems that a lot of the time some of the more interesting aspects of New York history are glossed over or mentioned as a passing reference. The story ends, as expected, with 9/11, and true, there is a poignant final note as the tale comes full circle - but as you close the book you cannot help feeling a little disappointed by what could have been.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8262287664174818533" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_77991162" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/77991162" />
    <a title="Tracy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1778396-tracy"><img alt="Tracy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589730806p2/1778396.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/77991162?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tracy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tracy" href="/user/show/1778396-tracy">Tracy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385521383" href="/book/show/6257535-new-york">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer77991162" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2635952641554762268">I love this book. So much so that I wrote an article about it. <br/><br/>... The author managed to tell not only the historical story of the city but also conveys the changes in mood, attitude, and life for New Yorkers over the centuries. For example, the way the characters relate to each other during the Revolutionary War, such as the concern for the whole rather than the individual, is vastly different from how they interact at the close of the book during the summer of 2009 and as it should be. The onl</span>
  <span id="freeText2635952641554762268" style="display:none">I love this book. So much so that I wrote an article about it. <br /><br />... The author managed to tell not only the historical story of the city but also conveys the changes in mood, attitude, and life for New Yorkers over the centuries. For example, the way the characters relate to each other during the Revolutionary War, such as the concern for the whole rather than the individual, is vastly different from how they interact at the close of the book during the summer of 2009 and as it should be. The only fault I have with the book is that the descendants of Quash the vanDyck's slave, Pale Feather, and Salvatore fell to the waste side in favor of the more traditional (and frankly easier to write) high society Master family. What became of Quash’s other descendants? Surely there could have been more to that side of the story than a tragic end during the NYC Draft Riots or Pale Feather’s family beyond the opening of the canal. <br /><br />For the rest of the review, please visit CBS Local New York after 1/19/15 at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://newyork.cbslocal.com/top-lists/best-books-based-in-new-york/">http://newyork.cbslocal.com/top-lists...</a> . </span>
  <a data-text-id="2635952641554762268" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1720980821" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1720980821" />
    <a title="Jim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36199787-jim"><img alt="Jim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1445213837p2/36199787.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1720980821?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jim" href="/user/show/36199787-jim">Jim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/7796349-new-york">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36199787-jim?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36199787-jim?shelf=books-read-2016">books-read-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1720980821" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2753549639232630271"><b>"People came here for freedom and, hard though the way up might be, they found it. To make it, you needed the work ethic."<br/><br/>"No matter how hard things were, New Yorkers never gave up."</b><br/><br/>This was a fascinating story that encompassed over 300 years. Starting in 1664 when present day New York City was a Dutch fort and trading post through 2009 as New Yorkers, and America, showed it's resilience following the terrorists attacks of September 11, 2001. There are many stories that make up this novel. Each </span>
  <span id="freeText2753549639232630271" style="display:none"><b>"People came here for freedom and, hard though the way up might be, they found it. To make it, you needed the work ethic."<br /><br />"No matter how hard things were, New Yorkers never gave up."</b><br /><br />This was a fascinating story that encompassed over 300 years. Starting in 1664 when present day New York City was a Dutch fort and trading post through 2009 as New Yorkers, and America, showed it's resilience following the terrorists attacks of September 11, 2001. There are many stories that make up this novel. Each story is from a different chapter in the history of this magnificent city. When the Dutch and native American Indians lived and worked together. When the seeds of independence from Britain were planted and you were either a Patriot or a Loyalist. When the country was torn apart by the Civil War and brother fought brother. Just because New York is in the north did not mean that everyone was an abolitionist. Sometimes there were splits within families. There were many tragedies and disasters throughout it's history. There were also many triumphs and accomplishments. Throughout New Yorkers persevered. <br /><br />This story centers mostly around the Master family who started as traders and later became bankers. They are the well to do. The blue bloods. The people with the money, nice houses, and everything that goes with their status. But this is just not about a well-to-do and successful family. New York is rich and culturally diverse. There are Italians, Irish, Germans, Jews, who came to New York. In this novel you read about some of these families who arrived at Ellis Island with little more than their clothing and who through hard work raised families and found success. <br /><br />What makes New York great is the people. The people who came for freedom and because they never gave up and worked hard found it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2753549639232630271" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_77680439" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/77680439" />
    <a title="Katherine Coble" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/295586-katherine-coble"><img alt="Katherine Coble" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1424895309p2/295586.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/77680439?book_show_action=true">Nov 13, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katherine Coble" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katherine Coble" href="/user/show/295586-katherine-coble">Katherine Coble</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385521383" href="/book/show/6257535-new-york">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer77680439" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10421925084468428302">It was only my love for Edward Rutherfurd in general that kept me slogging through this book. <br/><br/>Sarum was the book that converted me to a Rutherfrudite; it's still one of my all-time favourites. <br/><br/>That book was clearly more personal than New York, because Rutherfurd gave it both a strong sense of time and place that kept me riveted. His characters were part of the fabric of their time and place, and the story was memorably strong. <br/><br/><br/>New York, on the other hand, feels like a publisher's mandate to an a</span>
  <span id="freeText10421925084468428302" style="display:none">It was only my love for Edward Rutherfurd in general that kept me slogging through this book. <br /><br />Sarum was the book that converted me to a Rutherfrudite; it's still one of my all-time favourites. <br /><br />That book was clearly more personal than New York, because Rutherfurd gave it both a strong sense of time and place that kept me riveted. His characters were part of the fabric of their time and place, and the story was memorably strong. <br /><br /><br />New York, on the other hand, feels like a publisher's mandate to an author--"Keep up with the gimmick that makes us cash". There isn't much of a feel of the city in its old days. Sure, Rutherfurd tries to convince us (in the first 400 pages I think he mentions the 'gabled Dutch houses' about 50 times), but instead this book comes off like something that would happen if you did enough research into a place to fill your publisher's mandate but didn't actually care about it all that much. <br /><br />The real problem, though, started for me about the time of the War for Independence and continued right on through to the end. There is an off-putting pedanticness about this book, with Rutherfurd feeling the need to lecture to his readers about American History. When he brings up things like Lincoln's proposed resettlement of the freed slaves there is an undertone of arrogance, as though the author is saying "Ha! Betcha ignoramouses in America didn't know THAT!!!" <br /><br />I suppose if you are not a history buff, you won't feel as patronised as I did while reading this book. Then again, I suspect that a large share of his audience might be somewhat attuned to History, as that is the overarching theme of his works as a whole. <br /><br />I wanted to like this more because of how much I like him as an author. But I found myself unable to be convinced by New York, let alone swept away. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10421925084468428302" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385521383" href="/book/show/6257535-new-york">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer83094611" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14720433604030069928">It's a good book. But don't expect diversity in the story. Rutherford tailors his narrative pretty closely to the experiences of the Masters-to the detriment of the other families. Rutherford has chosen to avoid aspects of New York (Five Points/the Harlem Renaissance/the infant film industry/Broadway)that could have been mined for fascinating reading. It's the narrowness of the focus that really is the most frustrating aspect of the book. It's a good book, but it's not diverse.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13814942003376602792">American history is not my strength and I’m always on the look-out for books that will hold my interest me in this area. This one was wonderful, historically accurate, and beautifully written. I lived in New York when I was in graduate school many years ago. I appreciated learning about places and events that I knew very little about. The book starts with the 1600s Dutch settlers and Native Americans and goes all the way to the early 2000s. As you can imagine, it’s a massive read. It was such a </span>
  <span id="freeText13814942003376602792" style="display:none">American history is not my strength and I’m always on the look-out for books that will hold my interest me in this area. This one was wonderful, historically accurate, and beautifully written. I lived in New York when I was in graduate school many years ago. I appreciated learning about places and events that I knew very little about. The book starts with the 1600s Dutch settlers and Native Americans and goes all the way to the early 2000s. As you can imagine, it’s a massive read. It was such a good read that I didn’t want it to end. That’s saying a lot for a book that’s well over 800 pages. <br><br>New Amsterdam was renamed New York on September 8, 1664, in honor of the then Duke of York.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1580633575i/28890074._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The illustration below is an artist’s depiction of the stockade wall that would give its name to Wall Street. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1580633575i/28890075._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Today tourists stand in the spot where the Wall once stood. Behind them is the bronze statue of George Washington in front of Federal Hall National Memorial.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1580633575i/28890072._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Rutherfurd is an excellent writer. He wrote <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1979639528?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Paris</a> which I read a few years ago. He truly has a knack for making history come alive. You start rooting for various characters and truly caring for them. I plan to eventually read all his books. That’s how good of an author he is. <br><br>An encampment in New York City's Central Park, where many lived during the Great Depression.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1580633575i/28890073._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Here are some quotes that I thought are worth sharing:<br><br>“Whatever you do, keep your family together. That’s the most important thing in the world.”<br> <br>“If I had my life again, I’d act differently. It’s hard for a man if he thinks his wife doesn’t respect him.”<br><br>“Lincoln thinks slavery is wrong—that I don’t deny—but he went to war to preserve the Union. He made that perfectly clear. He has even said, in public: ‘If I could save the Union without freeing a single slave, I’d do it.’ His words. Not mine.” He paused. “What does Lincoln want for the slaves? Who knows? From what I hear, his main idea for liberated slaves is to find a free colony in Africa or Central America, and send them there. Do you know he actually told a delegation of black men, to their faces, that he doesn’t want Negroes in the United States?”<br><br>“I’d rather be the wife than the mistress.”<br>“You still have your marriage.”<br><br>“Marriage may not be a perfect state, but it is a protection, especially as we get older. And we are all getting older, my dear.” <br><br>“Many countries have accepted the Jews, … and always they have turned against them in the end. The Jews will only survive if they are strong. This is the lesson of history. … We were commanded to keep our faith. So let me tell you: every time a Jew marries out, we are weakened. Marry out, and in two, three generations, your family will not be Jewish. Maybe they will be safe, maybe not. But in the end, either way, all that we have will be lost.”<br><br>“I was reading Virginia Woolf the other day, and she remarked that at one period of her life, she was able to get so much done because she had three uninterrupted hours to work in every day. And I thought, what on earth is she talking about? Only three hours a day? And then I looked around the office at all the people working their fourteen-hour days, and I thought, how many of you actually spend three hours in real, creative, intellectual activity in a day? And I reckoned, probably not one.” She smiled. “And there’s Virginia Woolf achieving more than they ever will in their lives, on three hours a day. It makes you think. They might do better if they worked less.”<br><br>“You can do what you like, sir, but I'll tell you this. New York is the true capital of America. Every New Yorker knows it, and by God, we always shall.”<br><br>“All empires become arrogant. It is their nature.”<br><br>“She was quiet for a moment or two. Then she said: 'Cruel words are a terrible thing … Sometimes you regret them. But what's been said cannot be unsaid.”</span>

<div id="review_151142839" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/151142839" />
    <a title="Suzanne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3739451-suzanne"><img alt="Suzanne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1352731541p2/3739451.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/151142839?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Suzanne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Suzanne" href="/user/show/3739451-suzanne">Suzanne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385521383" href="/book/show/6257535-new-york">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3739451-suzanne?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3739451-suzanne?shelf=book-club-2012">book-club-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer151142839" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3180785164434094371">It’s no secret that Edward Rutherfurd is at the top of my list when it comes to favorite authors of historical fiction. I have been dying to read his latest <i>New York</i> since it first came out. I decided to wait, however, and put it on my book club reading list. Finally, the wait was over, and was it ever worth the wait!<br/><br/>In <i>New York</i>, Rutherfurd opens the novel in the year 1664, when the city was just a settlement called New Amsterdam. Like his other novels, the author takes a family or two, and carr</span>
  <span id="freeText3180785164434094371" style="display:none">It’s no secret that Edward Rutherfurd is at the top of my list when it comes to favorite authors of historical fiction. I have been dying to read his latest <i>New York</i> since it first came out. I decided to wait, however, and put it on my book club reading list. Finally, the wait was over, and was it ever worth the wait!<br /><br />In <i>New York</i>, Rutherfurd opens the novel in the year 1664, when the city was just a settlement called New Amsterdam. Like his other novels, the author takes a family or two, and carries their story forward in time. You follow them and watch how the historical events and the growth of the city affects them. In so doing, the reader has an opportunity to learn about history and, at the same time, is marvelously entertained with a sweeping, family saga.<br /><br />I think this book is Rutherfurd’s best. He has a way of seamlessly including historical events in a way that does not seem contrived. Even if you already know the history, be prepared to be surprised. The author knows how to capture your interest and keep you with him through the entire 862 pages. Unlike some of his previous novels, the jumps in time aren’t nearly so great here. That’s a plus, because I never felt I had to give up a character or a storyline before I was ready.<br /><br />I also really enjoyed the subject matter. Having lived in New York City for a number of years, I loved relearning some it’s history, and also being taught some things that I never knew about. My only complaint about the book was that it had to end. I really didn’t want it to.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3180785164434094371" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_260574120" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/260574120" />
    <a title="Shari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7405895-shari"><img alt="Shari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452635421p2/7405895.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/260574120?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shari" href="/user/show/7405895-shari">Shari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385521383" href="/book/show/6257535-new-york">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7405895-shari?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer260574120" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4898325380905468937">Like Rutherfurd’s other novels, New York: A Novel is a massive book. It would require dedication and time to read – also patience – for the story begins in the 17 century, during the Dutch colonization, to the 9/11 destruction of the World Trade Center in 2001. That’s 3 ½ centuries of history. Still, in spite of its length, the story didn’t linger very long in some eras. The author highlighted the most historic and momentous events: the coming of the British, the war of independence, the financi</span>
  <span id="freeText4898325380905468937" style="display:none">Like Rutherfurd’s other novels, New York: A Novel is a massive book. It would require dedication and time to read – also patience – for the story begins in the 17 century, during the Dutch colonization, to the 9/11 destruction of the World Trade Center in 2001. That’s 3 ½ centuries of history. Still, in spite of its length, the story didn’t linger very long in some eras. The author highlighted the most historic and momentous events: the coming of the British, the war of independence, the financial rise of the city, the Depression, urban decay, and many others. Right in the middle of these events is the Master family that witnessed and survived the tumultuous changes of the centuries. Along with them are other families, old and new, that help shape the history of the city. It was fascinating to read about how the families merge, part, and merge yet again over the centuries, and in their connection Rutherfurd included historical people – the Morgans, the Astors, the Stuyvesants, the Roosevelts. It was quite educational to know also how geography, politics in old Europe and powerful and simple families make the city become the financial capital of the country, how it becomes the city we know it is now. Money and wealth, constant elements of the novel from start to finish, show how New York City has been and will always be a city of the great American Dream. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4898325380905468937" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_85074193" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Jennifer (JC-S)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/283014-jennifer-jc-s"><img alt="Jennifer (JC-S)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528085840p2/283014.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/85074193?book_show_action=true">Jan 14, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer (JC-S)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer (JC-S)" href="/user/show/283014-jennifer-jc-s">Jennifer (JC-S)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer85074193" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8782846032510899256">‘New York is the true capital of America.’<br/>This novel begins, in 1664, with a tiny Indian village and Dutch traders. It ends in 2009 with an epilogue. In between, the journey through the generations of the fictional families Mr Rutherfurd has created traverses many of the major events in the history of both New York and America. <br/> <br/>From New Amsterdam as a Dutch trading settlement, through the period of British colonisation, and the War of Independence, the creation of the American nation, and the C</span>
  <span id="freeText8782846032510899256" style="display:none">‘New York is the true capital of America.’<br />This novel begins, in 1664, with a tiny Indian village and Dutch traders. It ends in 2009 with an epilogue. In between, the journey through the generations of the fictional families Mr Rutherfurd has created traverses many of the major events in the history of both New York and America. <br /> <br />From New Amsterdam as a Dutch trading settlement, through the period of British colonisation, and the War of Independence, the creation of the American nation, and the Civil War: these were the parts of the novel that held my attention most closely. This novel is about the evolution of New York, and the various families, characters and historical figures are important because they illuminate places, issues and times. This is not a history of New York, and some inaccuracies may aggravate those who spot them. <br /><br />While I enjoyed the novel, I found the characters less engaging towards the end. The earlier parts of the novel were well served by Mr Rutherfurd’s focus on the lives of families living through the historical events. By the end of the novel, the focus was almost entirely on one family and I found myself wondering about some of the others and the resolution of the issues they had been facing.<br /><br />I think that this novel primarily depicts the historical development of New York from an economic and political perspective, and this makes sense when looking at a city over a period of nearly 350 years. An absorbing work of historical fiction: I’m glad I read it.<br /><br />Jennifer Cameron-Smith<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8782846032510899256" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText8493071834644013332" style="display:none">INCREDIBLE. EPIC ENTERTAINMENT.<br /><br />I’ve long loved the City of New York. <span id="freeTextContainer1492466730144702519">Disappointing. Recommended by a friend whose taste I trust, but I couldn't finish it. John Masters is like an Early American Forrest Gump - not too bright and lots of famous people make cameo appearances in his life... Sam Adams, Ben Franklin, John Jay, etc. I stopped reading after about 250 pages and just skimmed bits to the end. I enjoyed Sarum and thought Rutherfurd was a good storyteller, but his writing seems really simplistic in New York and I was bored.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2054794125" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2054794125" />
    <a title="David" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3335664-david"><img alt="David" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551667298p2/3335664.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2054794125?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David" href="/user/show/3335664-david">David</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/8696944-new-york">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Dutch, Puritans, Irish, Italians, Germans, Jews, slaves, flappers, revolutionaries, survivors</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=american-history">american-history</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=doorstopper">doorstopper</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=new-york">new-york</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=18th-century">18th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=19th-century">19th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=17th-century">17th-century</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2054794125" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11576195343011067467"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1500165959i/23305678._SX540_.jpg' alt='Early New York' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I don't know how Edward Rutherfurd does the research to write these immense historical novels about different times and places. My first Rutherfurd novel was <i>Sarum</i>, which covered the entire history of England from the earliest Celts to the modern day. <i>New York</i> doesn't go back quite so far - only to the 1600s, and the beginnings of New York, but as with <i>Sarum</i>, it spans centuries of history by following the ups and downs of several families, who grow up in and with the city, sometimes leave and re</span>
  <span id="freeText11576195343011067467" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1500165959i/23305678._SX540_.jpg" alt="Early New York" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I don't know how Edward Rutherfurd does the research to write these immense historical novels about different times and places. My first Rutherfurd novel was <i>Sarum</i>, which covered the entire history of England from the earliest Celts to the modern day. <i>New York</i> doesn't go back quite so far - only to the 1600s, and the beginnings of New York, but as with <i>Sarum</i>, it spans centuries of history by following the ups and downs of several families, who grow up in and with the city, sometimes leave and return, sometimes are very much aware of their ancient lineage and sometimes have no idea when they are speaking to someone whose ancestors did business with their ancestors right in this same city. You, the reader, become attached to the Van Dycks, the Masters, the Kellers and the O'Donnells, all weaving their way through history and being joined by newer families along the way. All of the "main characters" in the book are fictional, but they meet with real historical figures, and experience historical events.<br><br>It's a grand, sweeping epic, driven by the melodramas of individual characters. We know that the Revolutionary War is coming, and how it will end, just as we know about the Civil War, and World Wars I and II, and in the final chapters of the novel, 9/11. But our fictional families go through it all as it happens.<br><br>The central figures in <i>New York</i>, the ones who are present through every generation, are the Van Dycks and the Masters. Originally Dutch and Puritan arrivals in New York, respectively, they intermarry and become one of the wealthy "old money" families of the city. At one point they reckon themselves at the top of the social order, but as the 19th century ends, even though they are still wealthy, they are being eclipsed by the Morgans, the Duponts, the Rockefellers, and in the early 20th century, wars and depressions reduce them to "genteel" circumstances. Still rich (as another character puts it, "What a strange world in which becoming poor meant moving to an apartment on Park Avenue!"), but now just rich compared to the average New Yorker. As the family's fortunes continue to wax and wane, they continue to be affluent, but still looking up at the titanic fortunes of investment bankers and dot.com billionaires.<br><br>There are also Irish and Jewish and Italian immigrant families who join the story. And here and there reappears the descendant of an Indian mistress who began the novel. Perhaps most tragic is the story of the descendants of Quash, the African slave, whose line also persists down through many generations until it is tragically cut short. Some families make it to the 21st century, some don't...<br><br>There were no uninteresting chapters. Whether it was the Dutch/English rivalries in early Manhattan, the conflict between Patriots and Loyalists as New York weathers the American Revolution, the draft riots of the Civil War era, the Flapper and Speakeasy era, the collapse of the economy in the Great Depression, the changing times of the 50s and 60s, or the turn of the 21st century, every era of history was illustrated not by an infodump about the historical events, but by returning to our friends the Masters, the Adlers, the Kellers, the Carusos, and seeing how they are faring.<br><br>I really love these books, and intend to eventually read all of Rutherfurd's novels. He's written several about England and Ireland, one about Russia, another about Paris. This is his style, to create relatable characters and then write them and their generations of descendent into a dramatic history that will probably dump a few things you didn't actually know on you along the way. Highly recommended for any fans of historical dramas.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11576195343011067467" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_714469382" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/714469382" />
    <a title="Marc  A." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1016435-marc-a"><img alt="Marc  A." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249391947p2/1016435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/714469382?book_show_action=true">Sep 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marc  A." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marc  A." href="/user/show/1016435-marc-a">Marc  A.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/7796349-new-york">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer714469382" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14777387839222819460">Another thoroughly enchanting and engaging historical fiction by Edward Rutherford. A master of the "James Michener School" of long, exhaustively researched, examinations of important historical places, achieved by creating compelling narratives at crucial points along the historical timeline that bring to life for the reader the place and the events that make it matter. <br/><br/>Some years ago, I read Rutherford's "London" in the hope that it would enhance my enjoyment of a then planned visit to the gre</span>
  <span id="freeText14777387839222819460" style="display:none">Another thoroughly enchanting and engaging historical fiction by Edward Rutherford. A master of the "James Michener School" of long, exhaustively researched, examinations of important historical places, achieved by creating compelling narratives at crucial points along the historical timeline that bring to life for the reader the place and the events that make it matter. <br /><br />Some years ago, I read Rutherford's "London" in the hope that it would enhance my enjoyment of a then planned visit to the great city, and I was rewarded beyond my wildest expectation. As a native New Yorker, I can say without hesitation, that anyone seeking to visit "The Big Apple" would do well to read this book first. Do not be put off by the length (860 pgs., incl. an epilogue, that surveys the history from New Amsterdam of 1664 - 2009,)because Rutherford is sucha magnificent storyteller, that you will be glad for the feeling that there is always a little more.<br /><br /> Finally I would point out that, though the book is clearly researched in depth, the author is not one of those who falls in love with their research to the detriment of the narrative flow. Moreover, Rutherford has an amazing ear for telling details that can only be gleaned from the most attentive reading and interviewing e.g. how could he know the importance of describing the layout of a Park Avenue Classic 6 apartment or even know about the "Wall St. gogo years" phenomenon (continuing to this day)of Bar/Bat Mitzvah extravaganza celebrations that often include Grucci-level fireworks displays and can cost hundreds of thousands of dollars? If you like a really yummy historical read, you won't be disappointed here. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14777387839222819460" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2638726737093236112">30 CDs. I think this is the longest audiobook I've ever listened to! I was trying to remember how long the Harry Potters were, but I think this one wins.<br/><br/>And, ohhhh, it was good. I love me a good epic, and Rutherfurd always delivers. This looooong adult novel covers the history of New York from the natives on Manhattan island to the fall of the World Trade Center. Several families are followed along the way, and the intertwining of them all makes the epic fascinating to follow. This kind of book </span>
  <span id="freeText2638726737093236112" style="display:none">30 CDs. I think this is the longest audiobook I've ever listened to! I was trying to remember how long the Harry Potters were, but I think this one wins.<br /><br />And, ohhhh, it was good. I love me a good epic, and Rutherfurd always delivers. This looooong adult novel covers the history of New York from the natives on Manhattan island to the fall of the World Trade Center. Several families are followed along the way, and the intertwining of them all makes the epic fascinating to follow. This kind of book is why readers like me score well on standardized tests--it's amazing how much a reader learns about history, the arts, political science, and just about everything else. The author is one heck of a storyteller. I loved his London, The Princes of Ireland, and Sarum, and I'll continue to read his new ones. I think he's a modern day Michener.</span>

<div id="review_155497055" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/155497055?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3773226830699692711">Fantastic; thoroughly enjoyed this book and made me want to go out and get his other ones. I love history and have had a fascination with New York since I was a little girl. The author weaves the stories of his fictional characters against the backdrop of all the major events in New York's past so easily, it's almost impossible to tell you're getting a history lesson at the same time. I will definitely be exploring Edward Rutherfurd's other books.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_462271128" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/462271128" />
    <a title="Lisa (Harmonybites)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2596042-lisa-harmonybites"><img alt="Lisa (Harmonybites)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1337396485p2/2596042.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/462271128?book_show_action=true">Nov 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa (Harmonybites)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa (Harmonybites)" href="/user/show/2596042-lisa-harmonybites">Lisa (Harmonybites)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385521383" href="/book/show/6257535-new-york">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Those Interested in New York City History and Historical Fiction</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Lisa (Harmonybites) by: </span>
      Suzanne Dobbins
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2596042-lisa-harmonybites?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2596042-lisa-harmonybites?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2596042-lisa-harmonybites?shelf=novels">novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2596042-lisa-harmonybites?shelf=literary-fiction">literary-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer462271128" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15036939212321408038">My first Rutherfurd work was <i>Sarum</i>, his novel telling the story of the history of England by focusing on five lineages down the centuries in the area around Stonehenge and Salisbury Cathedral. The style wasn’t anything special, even clunky at times, and with almost 9,000 years of history to cover, few characters ever felt fleshed out. It was a novel more broad than deep; it was <i>historical</i> fiction, almost more dramatized history text than stories with history as a backdrop. All of that can also b</span>
  <span id="freeText15036939212321408038" style="display:none">My first Rutherfurd work was <i>Sarum</i>, his novel telling the story of the history of England by focusing on five lineages down the centuries in the area around Stonehenge and Salisbury Cathedral. The style wasn’t anything special, even clunky at times, and with almost 9,000 years of history to cover, few characters ever felt fleshed out. It was a novel more broad than deep; it was <i>historical</i> fiction, almost more dramatized history text than stories with history as a backdrop. All of that can also be said of <i>New York: the Novel</i> which tries to encapsulate about 350 years of the history of New York City, mostly by following one family of English descent, the Masters, who early on married into one of the founding Dutch families, but as with <i>Sarum</i>, the effect is cumulative, and I found myself completely engaged through its 860 pages.<br /><br />I’m a native New Yorker, and as such so much of this book in the very beginning was irresistible. The book starts in 1664 when the population of New York City (New Amsterdam then) was only 1,500 people. I had a blast seeing all the Dutch Colonial origins of the name places around my city, some of which I knew (Wall Street, Canal Street, Harlem, Broadway, Manna hata, Bronck's land) and some not (Jonkers, Bouwerie, Pearl Street). The book, although focused on the Masters, also includes cameos by such historical figures as Peter Stuyvesant, Benjamin Franklin, George Washington, J. P. Morgan, Enrico Caruso. The chapters are almost more connected short stories than one united narrative with decades sometimes passing between them. I found among the most striking the early chapters, “New York” and “New Amsterdam” (Margarethe de Groot featured there was among the strongest female characters in the book), “The Patriot” and “Vanessa” which skillfully depicted the growing divide between the colonies and Mother country, “Draft” about the 1863 Draft Riots, “Old England” where an Irish family reinvents its past.<br /><br />Some reviewers complain the portrait of New York City isn’t diverse enough. I think that’s a casualty of Rutherford’s formula of trying to follow the history of the city through just a few families from the beginning, and particularly putting such emphasis on the Masters. I do feel <i>Sarum</i> did better in interweaving the various lineages over the centuries. Early in <i>New York</i> there was a thread about a family of African Americans. One early chapter was even written first person from the point of view of a slave in that family, but the African American story in the novel petered out and disappears after the Civil War. Irish and German immigrants don't come into the novel until after a good third of it has passed and Italians and Jews not until well after the half-way mark. Even though Rutherfurd mentions that there had been Jewish families in the city from the days of the Dutch, the novel doesn’t really deal with Jewish life in the city before the 1950s. I felt Rutherfurd missed an opportunity not making one such family a thread in his tapestry from the beginning, though I imagine he worried that might make things too unwieldy. He could have kept the Native American thread going too. Not many of the original Lenape are still here, that's true, but until recently there was a community of Mohawks in Brooklyn for over a century; a lot of Mohawks were involved in building our skyscrapers. No Asians are even mentioned until very late in the novel--there's nothing here about Chinatown at all. Centering the narrative on one family isn’t the best way to view such a dynamic, changing city. So many New Yorkers came from somewhere else, and few of us have roots that go deep: my father was born in Baltimore, Maryland, where his family had been for ages, my mother in rural Puerto Rico. <br /><br />My family’s own intersection with the city would only cover the last 150 pages of this multigenerational saga. It’s in the last chapters from the 1970s on where I can speak from personal experience I found weakest, that I thought rushed and where parts didn’t ring true. It’s a small thing, but he got wrong the details about the top three public high schools students could enter through competitive examination. Hunter high school would have still been an all girls school at the time his character Juan Campos could have attended. The three magnet public high schools in the sixties and beyond a boy could attend were Stuyvesant, Bronx Science--and Brooklyn Tech, not Hunter. I went to one of those schools--much later than Rutherford’s character would have, but no I can’t imagine Puerto Ricans being discouraged from trying or attending the way Rutherfurd presented it--not by that time anyway. There was nothing about the homeless problem that hit New York City in the 80s that was such a shock to me when I first saw it in my youth. (I recently read New York City is home to 14 percent of the national homeless population.) Nothing about how AIDs hit the vibrant gay community in New York (Gays and lesbians are almost invisible in this massive novel. There's just a brief mention in one of the last chapters of someone in one of the families being gay and of the Stonewall riot.) And Rutherford had only this to say about the Dinkins years: “Mayor Koch had been succeeded by Mayor Dinkins who, as an African American, had been perceived as more sympathetic to the troubles of Harlem and the other deprived areas.” Nothing about the Crown Heights riot that took place during those years that were a watershed for the city. Rutherford devotes a chapter to the 1977 blackouts, but not one line about what was, I think, as much a shock to New Yorkers. Mind you, it’s still a bitter, still a controversial event; I realize that. Dealing with it and its repercussions in New York City would have taken guts. But what else is fiction for? <br /><br />There are so many sides, so many strands to New York I pity anyone trying to tell our story. There was a lot in the book (including African American aspects) of the history of the city I never knew, so even a native like me felt I learned a lot. And a lot Rutherfurd got so very right. I couldn’t help smiling when John Master tells off a Thomas Jefferson determined to move the capital that, “New York is the true capital of America. Every New Yorker knows it, and by God we always will.” What proud New Yorker would disagree? In his introduction Rutherfurd called New York “a much-loved city.” His affection and respect for my city definitely came through.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15036939212321408038" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3122130475" />
    <a title="Tracy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25664087-tracy"><img alt="Tracy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1448924560p2/25664087.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3122130475?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tracy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tracy" href="/user/show/25664087-tracy">Tracy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3122130475" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1753343049454340805">This is my first book by Edward Rutherford and I listened to it as an audiobook. <br/><br/>The book starts in the 1600s with the native American Indians and Dutch settlers and moves through the American Revolution, the Civil War, the Gilded Age all the way through September 11th with the terrorist attack on the Twin Towers. You follow several families through all these times and all the different generations. <br/><br/>It's quite amazing and I enjoyed the story greatly!</span>

          </span>
        </div>
